<th scope="row">Website</th>
<td><span class="url"><a class="external text" href="http://uk.gov.in/" rel="nofollow">uk<wbr/>.gov<wbr/>.in</a></span></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left; font-size:smaller"><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_cap"><b><a href="#ref_cap">^a</a></b></span> Uttarakhand was formed by the <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh_Reorganisation_Act,_2000" title="Uttar Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2000">Uttar Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2000</a> with the bifurcation of erstwhile <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> on November 9, 2000.<br/>
<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_cap"><b><a href="#ref_cap">^b</a></b></span> Dehradun is the capital of Uttarakhand. The town of <a href="/wiki/Gairsain" title="Gairsain">Gairsain</a> is envisaged as the state's new capital.<br/>
<span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_cap"><b><a href="#ref_cap">^c</a></b></span> 70 seats are open for the direct election while 1 seat is reserved for the member of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo_Indian" title="Anglo Indian">Anglo Indian</a> community.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Uttarakhand</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">ˌ</span><span title="/ʊ/: 'oo' in 'foot'">ʊ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'r' in 'rye'">r</span><span title="/ɑː/: 'a' in 'father'">ɑː</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/ʌ/: 'u' in 'cut'">ʌ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap"> (<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-Uttarakhand.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="new" href="//en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:Upload?wpDestFile=En-Uttarakhand.ogg" title="En-Uttarakhand.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> officially the <b>State of Uttarakhand</b> (<i>Uttarākhaṇḍ Rājya</i>), formerly known as <b>Uttaranchal</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_India" title="States and territories of India">state</a> in the <a href="/wiki/North_India" title="North India">northern</a> part of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>. It is often referred to as the <i>Devbhumi</i><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> (literally "Land of the Gods") due to many <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindu</a> <a href="/wiki/Hindu_temple" title="Hindu temple">temples</a> and pilgrimage centres found throughout the state. Uttarakhand is known for the natural environment of the <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Bhabar" title="Bhabar">Bhabhar</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Terai" title="Terai">Terai</a>. On 9 November 2000, Uttarakhand became the 27th state of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_India" title="Republic of India">Republic of India</a>, being created from the Himalayan and adjoining northwestern districts of <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> It borders <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> to the north; the <a href="/wiki/Mahakali_Zone" title="Mahakali Zone">Mahakali Zone</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Far-Western_Region,_Nepal" title="Far-Western Region, Nepal">Far-Western Region</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> to the east; and the Indian states of <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> to the south and <a href="/wiki/Himachal_Pradesh" title="Himachal Pradesh">Himachal Pradesh</a> to the west and north-west as well as <a href="/wiki/Haryana" title="Haryana">Haryana</a> on its south-western corner. The state is divided into two divisions, <a href="/wiki/Garhwal_division" title="Garhwal division">Garhwal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kumaon_division" title="Kumaon division">Kumaon</a>, with a total of <a href="/wiki/List_of_districts_of_Uttarakhand" title="List of districts of Uttarakhand">13 districts</a>. The interim capital of Uttarakhand is <a href="/wiki/Dehradun" title="Dehradun">Dehradun</a>, the largest city of the state, which is a railhead. The <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_High_Court" title="Uttarakhand High Court">High Court</a> of the state is located in <a href="/wiki/Nainital" title="Nainital">Nainital</a>.</p>
<p>Archaeological evidence supports the existence of humans in the region since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prehistoric_times" title="Prehistoric times">prehistoric times</a>. The region formed a part of the <a href="/wiki/Kuru_Kingdom" title="Kuru Kingdom">Kuru</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Panchala" title="Panchala">Panchal</a> kingdoms (<i><a href="/wiki/Mahajanapada" title="Mahajanapada">mahajanpads</a></i>) during the <a href="/wiki/Vedic_period" title="Vedic period">Vedic age</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_India" title="Ancient India">Ancient India</a>. Among the first major dynasties of Kumaon were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kuninda" title="Kuninda">Kunindas</a> in the 2nd century BCE who practised an early form of <a href="/wiki/Shaivism" title="Shaivism">Shaivism</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Ashokan</a> edicts at <a href="/wiki/Kalsi" title="Kalsi">Kalsi</a> show the early presence of <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> in this region. During the medieval period, the region was consolidated under the <a href="/wiki/Kumaon_Kingdom" title="Kumaon Kingdom">Kumaon Kingdom</a> and <a href="/wiki/Garhwal_Kingdom" title="Garhwal Kingdom">Garhwal Kingdom</a>. In 1816, most of modern Uttarakhand was ceded to the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Sugauli" title="Treaty of Sugauli">Treaty of Sugauli</a>. Although the erstwhile hill kingdoms of Garhwal and Kumaon were traditional rivals, the proximity of different neighboring ethnic groups and the inseparable and complementary nature of their geography, economy, culture, language, and traditions created strong bonds between the two regions which further strengthened during the <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_movement" title="Uttarakhand movement">Uttarakhand movement</a> for statehood in the 1990s.</p>
<p>The natives of the state are generally called Uttarakhandi, or more specifically either Garhwali or Kumaoni by their region of origin. According to the <a href="/wiki/2011_Census_of_India" title="2011 Census of India">2011 Census of India</a>, Uttarakhand has a population of 10,086,292, making it the 19th <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_and_union_territories_of_India_by_population" title="List of states and union territories of India by population">most populous state</a> in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Uttarakhand's name is derived from the Sanskrit words <i>uttara</i> (<span lang="sa">उत्तर</span>) meaning 'north', and <i>khaṇḍa</i> (<span lang="sa">खण्ड</span>) meaning 'land', altogether simply meaning 'Northern Land'. The name finds mention in early <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hindu_scriptures" title="Hindu scriptures">Hindu scriptures</a> as the combined region of "Kedarkhand" (present day <a href="/wiki/Garhwal_division" title="Garhwal division">Garhwal</a>) and "Manaskhand" (present day <a href="/wiki/Kumaon_division" title="Kumaon division">Kumaon</a>). Uttarakhand was also the ancient <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puranic" title="Puranic">Puranic</a> (<span lang="sa">पौराणिक</span>) term for the central stretch of the Indian <a href="/wiki/Himalayas" title="Himalayas">Himalayas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2001_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2001-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>However, the region was given the name <i>Uttaranchal</i> by the <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a> led central government and <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a> state government when they started a new round of state reorganisation in 1998. Chosen for its allegedly less separatist connotations, the name change generated enormous controversy among many activists for a separate state who saw it as a political act.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> The name Uttarakhand remained popular in the region, even while Uttaranchal was promulgated through official usage.</p>
<p>In August 2006, Union Cabinet of India assented to the demands of the Uttaranchal state assembly and leading members of the <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_movement" title="Uttarakhand movement">Uttarakhand statehood movement</a> to rename Uttaranchal state as Uttarakhand. Legislation to that effect was passed by the <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Legislative_Assembly" title="Uttarakhand Legislative Assembly">Uttarakhand Legislative Assembly</a> in October 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and the Union Cabinet brought in the bill in the winter session of Parliament. The bill was passed by Parliament and signed into law by then President <a href="/wiki/A._P._J._Abdul_Kalam" title="A. P. J. Abdul Kalam">A. P. J. Abdul Kalam</a> in December 2006, and since January 1, 2007 the state has been known as Uttarakhand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Uttarakhand" title="History of Uttarakhand">History of Uttarakhand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_movement" title="Uttarakhand movement">Uttarakhand movement</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jageshwar_main.JPG"><img alt="Historical temples at Jageshwar" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="960" data-file-width="1280" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Jageshwar_main.JPG/290px-Jageshwar_main.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Jageshwar_main.JPG/435px-Jageshwar_main.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Jageshwar_main.JPG/580px-Jageshwar_main.JPG 2x" width="290"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jageshwar_main.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The historical temples at <a href="/wiki/Jageshwar" title="Jageshwar">Jageshwar</a>, preserved by the <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_Survey_of_India" title="Archaeological Survey of India">Archaeological Survey of India</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Ancient rock paintings, rock shelters, <a href="/wiki/Paleolithic" title="Paleolithic">paleolithic</a> stone tools (hundreds of thousands of years old), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Megaliths" title="Megaliths">megaliths</a> provide evidence that the mountains of the region have been inhabited since prehistoric times. There are also archaeological remains which show the existence of early <a href="/wiki/Vedic_period" title="Vedic period">Vedic</a> (c. 1500 BCE) practices in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-13">[13]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paurava" title="Paurava">Pauravas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kushan_Empire" title="Kushan Empire">Kushanas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kuninda_Kingdom" title="Kuninda Kingdom">Kunindas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gupta_Empire" title="Gupta Empire">Guptas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gurjara-Pratihara" title="Gurjara-Pratihara">Gurjara-Pratihara</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Katyuri_Kings" title="Katyuri Kings">Katyuris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Doti" title="Doti">Raikas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pala_Empire" title="Pala Empire">Palas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chand_Kings" title="Chand Kings">Chands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Parmar" title="Parmar">Parmars</a> or Panwars, and the <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">British</a> have ruled Uttarakhand in turns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2001_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2001-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The region was originally settled by <a href="/wiki/Kol_people" title="Kol people">Kol people</a>, an aboriginal people of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Asiatic" title="Austro-Asiatic">Austro-Asiatic</a> physical type who were later joined by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Aryans" title="Indo-Aryans">Indo-Aryan</a> <a href="/wiki/Khasas" title="Khasas">Khasas</a> tribe that arrived from the northwest by the Vedic period (1700–1100 BCE). At that time, present-day Uttarakhand also served as a habitat for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rishis" title="Rishis">Rishis</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sadhus" title="Sadhus">Sadhus</a>. It is believed that the sage <a href="/wiki/Vyasa" title="Vyasa">Vyasa</a> scripted the Hindu epic <i><a href="/wiki/Mahabharata" title="Mahabharata">Mahabharata</a></i> in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-epic_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-epic-14">[14]</a></sup> Among the first major dynasties of Garhwal and Kumaon were the Kunindas in the 2nd century BCE who practised an early form of <a href="/wiki/Shaivism" title="Shaivism">Shaivism</a> and traded salt with Western <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a>. It is evident from the <a href="/wiki/Ashoka" title="Ashoka">Ashokan</a> edict at <a href="/wiki/Kalsi" title="Kalsi">Kalsi</a> in Western Garhwal that <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> made inroads in this region. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shamanic" title="Shamanic">Folk shamanic</a> practices deviating from Hindu orthodoxy also persisted here. However, Garhwal and Kumaon were restored to nominal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vedic_Brahmanism" title="Vedic Brahmanism">Hindu</a> rule due to the travails of <a href="/wiki/Shankaracharya" title="Shankaracharya">Shankaracharya</a> and the arrival of migrants from the plains.</p>
<p>Between the 4th and 14th centuries, the Katyuri dynasty dominated lands of varying extent from the Katyur (modern day <a href="/wiki/Baijnath,_Uttarakhand" title="Baijnath, Uttarakhand">Baijnath</a>) valley in Kumaon. The historically significant temples at <a href="/wiki/Jageshwar" title="Jageshwar">Jageshwar</a> are believed to have been built by the Katyuris and later remodelled by the Chands. Other peoples of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman" title="Tibeto-Burman">Tibeto-Burman</a> group known as <a href="/wiki/Kirata" title="Kirata">Kirata</a> are thought to have settled in the northern highlands as well as in pockets throughout the region, and are believed to be ancestors of the modern day <a href="/wiki/Bhotiya" title="Bhotiya">Bhotiya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raji_people" title="Raji people">Raji</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buksa_people" title="Buksa people">Buksa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tharu_people" title="Tharu people">Tharu</a> people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Tehri_Garhwal.svg"><img alt="Princely flag of Garhwal Kingdom" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="920" height="87" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Tehri_Garhwal.svg/200px-Flag_of_Tehri_Garhwal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Tehri_Garhwal.svg/300px-Flag_of_Tehri_Garhwal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9a/Flag_of_Tehri_Garhwal.svg/400px-Flag_of_Tehri_Garhwal.svg.png 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Tehri_Garhwal.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Princely flag of <a href="/wiki/Garhwal_Kingdom" title="Garhwal Kingdom">Kingdom of Garhwal</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>By the medieval period, the region was consolidated under the <a href="/wiki/Garhwal_Kingdom" title="Garhwal Kingdom">Garhwal Kingdom</a> in the west and the <a href="/wiki/Kumaon_Kingdom" title="Kumaon Kingdom">Kumaon Kingdom</a> in the east. During this period, learning and new forms of painting (the <a href="/wiki/Pahari_painting" title="Pahari painting">Pahari</a> school of art) developed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> Modern-day Garhwal was likewise unified under the rule of Parmars who, along with many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brahmins" title="Brahmins">Brahmins</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rajputs" title="Rajputs">Rajputs</a>, also arrived from the plains.,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> the seat of the Kumaon Kingdom. The Garhwal Kingdom was re-established from a smaller region in <a href="/wiki/Tehri" title="Tehri">Tehri</a>. It was annexed to Kingdom of Nepal by <a href="/wiki/Amar_Singh_Thapa" title="Amar Singh Thapa">Amar Singh Thapa</a>. After <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Nepalese_War" title="Anglo-Nepalese War">Anglo-Nepalese War</a>, it was ceded to the British as part of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Sugauli" title="Treaty of Sugauli">Treaty of Sugauli</a>.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:United_Provinces_1903.gif"><img alt="Map of Uttarakhand as part of United Province" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/United_Provinces_1903.gif/200px-United_Provinces_1903.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/United_Provinces_1903.gif/300px-United_Provinces_1903.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/United_Provinces_1903.gif/400px-United_Provinces_1903.gif 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:United_Provinces_1903.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Uttarakhand as a part of the <a href="/wiki/United_Provinces_of_Agra_and_Oudh" title="United Provinces of Agra and Oudh">United Province</a>, 1903</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After India attained independence from the British, the Garhwal Kingdom was merged into the state of <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh" title="Uttar Pradesh">Uttar Pradesh</a>, where Uttarakhand composed the Garhwal and Kumaon Divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Until 1998, Uttarakhand was the name most commonly used to refer to the region, as various political groups, including the <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Kranti_Dal" title="Uttarakhand Kranti Dal">Uttarakhand Kranti Dal</a> (Uttarakhand Revolutionary Party), began agitating for separate statehood under its banner. Although the erstwhile hill kingdoms of Garhwal and Kumaon were traditional rivals the inseparable and complementary nature of their geography, economy, culture, language, and traditions created strong bonds between the two regions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> These bonds formed the basis of the new political identity of Uttarakhand, which gained significant momentum in 1994, when demand for separate statehood achieved almost unanimous acceptance among both the local populace and national political parties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most notable incident during this period was the <a href="/wiki/Rampur_Tiraha_firing_case" title="Rampur Tiraha firing case">Rampur Tiraha firing case</a> on the night of 1 October 1994, which led to a public uproar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> On 24 September 1998, the <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh_Legislative_Assembly" title="Uttar Pradesh Legislative Assembly">Uttar Pradesh Legislative Assembly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh_Legislative_Council" title="Uttar Pradesh Legislative Council">Uttar Pradesh Legislative Council</a> passed the Uttar Pradesh Reorganisation Bill, which began the process of creating a new state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> Two years later the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_India" title="Parliament of India">Parliament of India</a> passed the <a href="/wiki/Uttar_Pradesh_Reorganisation_Act,_2000" title="Uttar Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2000">Uttar Pradesh Reorganisation Act, 2000</a> and thus, on 9 November 2000, Uttarakhand became the 27th state of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Republic_of_India" title="Republic of India">Republic of India</a>.</p>
<table class="rquote floatleft" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:left; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">
<tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;"><span lang="hi">माटू हमरू, पाणी हमरू, हमरा ही छन यी बौण भी... पितरों न लगाई बौण, हमुनही त बचौण भी</span>।<br/>
Soil ours, water ours, ours are these forests. Our forefathers raised them, it's we who must protect them.<br/>
<small>—<i>Old Chipko Song</i> (<a href="/wiki/Garhwali_language" title="Garhwali language">Garhwali language</a>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teh_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-teh-23">[23]</a></sup></small></td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:'Times New Roman',serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">”</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:1em; text-align:right;"></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Uttarakhand is also well known for the mass agitation of the 1970s that led to the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Chipko_movement" title="Chipko movement">Chipko environmental movement</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> and other social movements. Though primarily a <a href="/wiki/Livelihood" title="Livelihood">livelihood</a> movement rather than a forest conservation movement, it went on to become a rallying point for many future <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmentalists" title="Environmentalists">environmentalists</a>, environmental protests, and movements the world over and created a precedent for non-violent protest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> It stirred up the existing civil society in India, which began to address the issues of tribal and marginalized people. So much so that, a quarter of a century later, <i><a href="/wiki/India_Today" title="India Today">India Today</a></i> mentioned the people behind the "forest satyagraha" of the Chipko movement as amongst "100 people who shaped India".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ITD_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-ITD-26">[26]</a></sup> One of Chipko's most salient features was the mass participation of female villagers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Both female and male activists played pivotal roles in the movement. Gaura Devi was the main activist who started this movement other participants were <a href="/wiki/Chandi_Prasad_Bhatt" title="Chandi Prasad Bhatt">Chandi Prasad Bhatt</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sundarlal_Bahuguna" title="Sundarlal Bahuguna">Sundarlal Bahuguna</a>, and Ghanshyam Raturi, the popular Chipko poet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Uttarakhand" title="Geography of Uttarakhand">Geography of Uttarakhand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nanda_devi.jpg"><img alt="Mountain of Nanda Devi" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="682" data-file-width="1024" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Nanda_devi.jpg/250px-Nanda_devi.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Nanda_devi.jpg/375px-Nanda_devi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Nanda_devi.jpg/500px-Nanda_devi.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nanda_devi.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
With the elevation of 7,816 metres (25,643 ft) above sea level, <a href="/wiki/Nanda_Devi" title="Nanda Devi">Nanda Devi</a> is the highest mountain in Uttarakhand and the second-highest mountain in India, following <a href="/wiki/Kangchenjunga" title="Kangchenjunga">Kangchenjunga</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sikkim" title="Sikkim">Sikkim</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Uttarakhand has a total area of 53,483 km<sup>2</sup>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uttarakhand_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-Uttarakhand-29">[29]</a></sup> of which 86% is mountainous and 65% is covered by <a href="/wiki/Forest" title="Forest">forest</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uttarakhand_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-Uttarakhand-29">[29]</a></sup> Most of the northern part of the state is covered by high <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Himalaya" title="Himalaya">Himalayan</a> peaks and glaciers. In the first half of the nineteenth century, the expanding development of Indian roads, railways and other physical infrastructure was giving rise to concerns over indiscriminate logging, particularly in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Himalaya" title="Himalaya">Himalaya</a>. Two of the most important rivers in Hinduism originate in the glaciers of Uttarakhand, the <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">Ganges</a> at <a href="/wiki/Gangotri" title="Gangotri">Gangotri</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Yamuna" title="Yamuna">Yamuna</a> at <a href="/wiki/Yamunotri" title="Yamunotri">Yamunotri</a>. They are fed by myriad lakes, glacial melts and streams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> These two along with <a href="/wiki/Badrinath" title="Badrinath">Badrinath</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kedarnath" title="Kedarnath">Kedarnath</a> form the <a href="/wiki/Chota_Char_Dham" title="Chota Char Dham">Chota Char Dham</a>, a holy pilgrimage for the Hindus.</p>
<p>The state hosts the <a href="/wiki/Bengal_tiger" title="Bengal tiger">Bengal tiger</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jim_Corbett_National_Park" title="Jim Corbett National Park">Jim Corbett National Park</a>, the oldest national park of the Indian subcontinent. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valley_of_Flowers" title="Valley of Flowers">Valley of Flowers</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a> located in the upper expanses of Bhyundar Ganga near <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joshimath" title="Joshimath">Joshimath</a> in Gharwal region, is known for the variety and rarity of its flowers and plants.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> One who raised this was Sir <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Dalton_Hooker" title="Joseph Dalton Hooker">Joseph Dalton Hooker</a>, Director of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Botanic_Gardens,_Kew" title="Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew">Royal Botanic Gardens, Kew</a>, who visited the region. As a consequence, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lord_Dalhousie" title="Lord Dalhousie">Lord Dalhousie</a> issued the Indian Forest Charter in 1855, reversing the previous laissez-faire policy. The following Indian Forest Act of 1878 put Indian forestry on a solid scientific basis. A direct consequence was the founding of the Imperial Forest School at <a href="/wiki/Dehradun" title="Dehradun">Dehradun</a> by <a href="/wiki/Dietrich_Brandis" title="Dietrich Brandis">Dietrich Brandis</a> in 1878. Renamed the 'Imperial Forest Research Institute' in 1906, it is now known as the <a href="/wiki/Forest_Research_Institute_(India)" title="Forest Research Institute (India)">Forest Research Institute (India)</a>.</p>
<p>The model “Forest Circles” around Dehradun, used for training, demonstration and scientific measurements, had a lasting positive influence on the forests and ecology of the region. The Himalayan ecosystem provides habitat for many animals (including <a href="/wiki/Bharal" title="Bharal">bharal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Snow_leopard" title="Snow leopard">snow leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopards</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tiger" title="Tiger">tigers</a>), plants, and rare herbs.</p>
<p>Uttarakhand lies on the southern slope of the Himalaya range, and the climate and vegetation vary greatly with elevation, from glaciers at the highest elevations to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical" title="Subtropical">subtropical</a> forests at the lower elevations. The highest elevations are covered by ice and bare rock. Below them, between 3,000 and 5,000 metres (9,800 and 16,400 ft) are the <a href="/wiki/Western_Himalayan_alpine_shrub_and_meadows" title="Western Himalayan alpine shrub and meadows">western Himalayan alpine shrub and meadows</a>. The temperate <a href="/wiki/Western_Himalayan_subalpine_conifer_forests" title="Western Himalayan subalpine conifer forests">western Himalayan subalpine conifer forests</a> grow just below the tree line. At 3,000 to 2,600 metres (9,800 to 8,500 ft) elevation they transition to the temperate <a href="/wiki/Western_Himalayan_broadleaf_forests" title="Western Himalayan broadleaf forests">western Himalayan broadleaf forests</a>, which lie in a belt from 2,600 to 1,500 metres (8,500 to 4,900 ft) elevation. Below 1,500 metres (4,900 ft) elevation lie the <a href="/wiki/Himalayan_subtropical_pine_forests" title="Himalayan subtropical pine forests">Himalayan subtropical pine forests</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Upper_Gangetic_Plains_moist_deciduous_forests" title="Upper Gangetic Plains moist deciduous forests">Upper Gangetic Plains moist deciduous forests</a> and the drier <a href="/wiki/Terai-Duar_savanna_and_grasslands" title="Terai-Duar savanna and grasslands">Terai-Duar savanna and grasslands</a> cover the lowlands along the Uttar Pradesh border in a belt locally known as <a href="/wiki/Bhabar" title="Bhabar">Bhabar</a>. These lowland forests have mostly been cleared for agriculture, but a few pockets remain.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>In June 2013 several days of extremely heavy rain caused <a href="/wiki/2013_North_India_floods" title="2013 North India floods">devastating floods</a> in the region, resulting in more than 5000 people missing and presumed dead. The flooding was referred to in the Indian media as a "Himalayan Tsunami".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>The native people of Uttarakhand are generally called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uttarakhandi" title="Uttarakhandi">Uttarakhandi</a> and sometimes specifically either <a href="/wiki/Garhwali_people" title="Garhwali people">Garhwali</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kumaoni_people" title="Kumaoni people">Kumaoni</a> depending on their place of origin in either the <a href="/wiki/Garhwal_division" title="Garhwal division">Garhwal</a> or <a href="/wiki/Kumaon_division" title="Kumaon division">Kumaon</a> region. According to the <a href="/wiki/2011_Census_of_India" title="2011 Census of India">2011 Census of India</a>, Uttarakhand has a population of 10,086,292 comprising 5,137,773 males and 4,948,519 females, with 69.77% of the population living in rural areas. The state is the 20th most populous state of the country having 0.83% of the population on 1.63% of the land. The population density of the state is 189 people per square kilometre having a 2001–2011 decadal growth rate of 18.81%. The gender ratio is 963 females per 1000 males.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-census-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demography_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Demography-37">[37]</a></sup> The crude birth rate in the state is 18.6 with the <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> being 2.3. The state has an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Infant_mortality_rate" title="Infant mortality rate">infant mortality rate</a> of 43, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality_rate" title="Maternal mortality rate">maternal mortality rate</a> of 188 and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crude_death_rate" title="Crude death rate">crude death rate</a> of 6.6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Uttarakhand has a multiethnic population spread across two geocultural regions: the Garhwal, and the Kumaon. A large portion of the population is <a href="/wiki/Rajput" title="Rajput">Rajput</a> (various clans of erstwhile landowning rulers and their descendants), including members of the native <a href="/wiki/Garhwali_people" title="Garhwali people">Garhwali</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kumaoni_people" title="Kumaoni people">Kumaoni</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gujjar" title="Gujjar">Gujjar</a> communities, as well as a number of immigrants. According to a 2007 study by <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_the_Study_of_Developing_Societies" title="Centre for the Study of Developing Societies">Centre for the Study of Developing Societies</a>, Uttarakhand has the highest percentage of <a href="/wiki/Brahmin" title="Brahmin">Brahmins</a> of any state in India, with approximately 20% of the population being Brahmin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> 18.76% of the population belongs to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scheduled_Castes" title="Scheduled Castes">Scheduled Castes</a> (an official term for the lower castes in the traditional <a href="/wiki/Caste_system_in_India" title="Caste system in India">Hindu caste system</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demography_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Demography-37">[37]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scheduled_Tribes" title="Scheduled Tribes">Scheduled Tribes</a> (an official term for natives outside the Indian social system), such as the <a href="/wiki/Tharu_people" title="Tharu people">Tharu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jaunsari_people" title="Jaunsari people">Jaunsari</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buksa_people" title="Buksa people">Buksa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Bhotiya" title="Uttarakhand Bhotiya">Bhotiya</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raji_people" title="Raji people">Raji</a> constitute 2.89% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demography_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-Demography-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>Languages in Uttarakhand (2001)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2011lang_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-2011lang-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> (87.95%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Purple; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a> (5.86%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Punjabi_language" title="Punjabi language">Punjabi</a> (2.91%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Red; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a> (1.45%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Blue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a> (1.07%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Grey; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Other (0.76%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a> belonging to <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan languages</a> is the sole official language of Uttarakhand and is spoken by 87.95% of the population (figure includes the <a href="/wiki/Pahari_languages" title="Pahari languages">Pahari languages</a>; <a href="/wiki/Garhwali_language" title="Garhwali language">Garhwali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kumaoni_language" title="Kumaoni language">Kumaoni</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jaunsari_language" title="Jaunsari language">Jaunsari</a> as variants of Hindi). <a href="/wiki/Sanskrit" title="Sanskrit">Sanskrit</a> is given the status of second official language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sanskrit_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-sanskrit-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sanskrit2_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-sanskrit2-3">[3]</a></sup> Many <a href="/wiki/Tibeto-Burman_languages" title="Tibeto-Burman languages">Tibeto-Burman languages</a> are also spoken in this region, including <a href="/wiki/Sherpa_language" title="Sherpa language">Bhoti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jad_language" title="Jad language">Jad</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rangkas_language" title="Rangkas language">Rangkas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Darmiya_language" title="Darmiya language">Darmiya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byangsi_language" title="Byangsi language">Byangsi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chaudangsi_language" title="Chaudangsi language">Chaudangsi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright" style="">

<p>Religion in Uttarakhand (2011)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census2011_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-census2011-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Orange; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> (82.97%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Green; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> (13.95%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DarkKhaki; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Sikhism" title="Sikhism">Sikhism</a> (2.34%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:DodgerBlue; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> (0.37%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhism</a> (0.15%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Brown; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> <a href="/wiki/Jainism" title="Jainism">Jainism</a> (0.09%)</div>
<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color:Black; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;"> </span> Other or not religious (0.13%)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>More than four-fifths of Uttarakhand’s residents are Hindus.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-13">[13]</a></sup> Muslims, Sikhs, Christians, Buddhists, and Jains make up the remaining population with the Muslims being the largest minority.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demography_37-3"><a href="#cite_note-Demography-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Uttarakhand" title="Government of Uttarakhand">Government of Uttarakhand</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Legislature_of_Uttarakhand" title="Legislature of Uttarakhand">Legislature of Uttarakhand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Uttarakhand" title="Elections in Uttarakhand">Elections in Uttarakhand</a></div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_India" title="Constitution of India">Constitution of India</a>, Uttarakhand, like all Indian states, has a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary system</a> of <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a> for its government.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Governors_of_states_of_India" title="Governors of states of India">Governor</a> is the constitutional and formal head of the government and is appointed for a five-year term by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_India" title="President of India">President of India</a> on the advice of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Union government</a>. The present Governor of the state is <a href="/wiki/Krishan_Kant_Paul" title="Krishan Kant Paul">Krishan Kant Paul</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_(India)" title="Chief Minister (India)">Chief Minister</a>, who holds the real executive powers, is the head of the party or coalition garnering the majority in the state elections. The current Chief Minister of Uttarakhand is <a href="/wiki/Trivendra_Singh_Rawat" title="Trivendra Singh Rawat">Trivendra Singh Rawat</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Legislative_Assembly" title="Uttarakhand Legislative Assembly">Uttarakhand Legislative Assembly</a> consists of has 71 elected members, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Members_of_the_Legislative_Assembly" title="Members of the Legislative Assembly">Members of the Legislative Assembly</a> or MLAs,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uttarakhand_Legislative_Assembly_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Uttarakhand_Legislative_Assembly-42">[42]</a></sup> and special office bearers such as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Speakers_of_the_Uttarakhand_Legislative_Assembly" title="List of Speakers of the Uttarakhand Legislative Assembly">Speaker</a> and Deputy Speaker, elected by the members. Assembly meetings are presided over by the Speaker, or the Deputy Speaker in the Speaker's absence. A <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Council_of_Ministers" title="Uttarakhand Council of Ministers">Council of Ministers</a> is appointed by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Governor_of_Uttarakhand" title="Governor of Uttarakhand">Governor of Uttarakhand</a> on the advice of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Uttarakhand" title="Chief Minister of Uttarakhand">Chief Minister of Uttarakhand</a> and reports to the Legislative Assembly. Auxiliary authorities that govern at a local level are known as panchayats in rural areas, municipalities in urban areas and municipal corporation in metro areas. All state and local government offices have a five-year term. The state also elects 5 members to <a href="/wiki/Lok_Sabha" title="Lok Sabha">Lok Sabha</a> and 3 seats to <a href="/wiki/Rajya_Sabha" title="Rajya Sabha">Rajya Sabha</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Parliament" title="Indian Parliament">Indian Parliament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The judiciary consists of the <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_High_Court" title="Uttarakhand High Court">Uttarakhand High Court</a>, located at <a href="/wiki/Nainital" title="Nainital">Nainital</a>, and a system of lower courts. The present <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chief_Justices_of_the_Uttarakhand_High_Court" title="List of Chief Justices of the Uttarakhand High Court">Chief Justice of Uttarakhand</a> is Justice <a href="/wiki/K._M._Joseph" title="K. M. Joseph">K. M. Joseph</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Politics in Uttarakhand is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">Indian National Congress</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Bharatiya_Janata_Party" title="Bharatiya Janata Party">Bharatiya Janata Party</a>. Since the formation of the state these parties have ruled the state in turns. Following the hung mandate in the <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Legislative_Assembly_election,_2012" title="Uttarakhand Legislative Assembly election, 2012">Uttarakhand Legislative Assembly election, 2012</a>, the Indian National Congress, having the maximum number of seats, formed a coalition government headed by <a href="/wiki/Harish_Rawat" title="Harish Rawat">Harish Rawat</a> that collapsed on 27 March 2016, following the political turmoil as about nine <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLAs" title="MLAs">MLAs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">INC</a> rebelled against the party and supported the opposition party <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BJP" title="BJP">BJP</a>, causing Harish Rawat government to lose the majority in assembly. However, on 21 April 2016 the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Uttarakhand" title="High Court of Uttarakhand">High Court of Uttarakhand</a> quashed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President%27s_Rule" title="President's Rule">President's Rule</a> questioning its legality and maintained a status quo prior to 27 March 2016 when 9 rebel <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLAs" title="MLAs">MLAs</a> of <a href="/wiki/Indian_National_Congress" title="Indian National Congress">INC</a> voted against the <a href="/wiki/Harish_Rawat" title="Harish Rawat">Harish Rawat</a> government in assembly on state's money appropriation bill. This has been seen as a big blow to central government which is expected to take the matter to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_India" title="Supreme Court of India">Supreme Court of India</a> to challenge the verdict of High Court. On 22 April 2016 the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_India" title="Supreme Court of India">Supreme Court of India</a> stayed the order of High Court till 27 April 2016, thereby once again reviving the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/President%27s_Rule" title="President's Rule">President's Rule</a>. In later developments regarding this matter, the Supreme Court ordered a floor test to be held on 10 May with the rebels being barred from voting. On 11 May at the opening of sealed result of the floor test, under the supervision of Supreme Court, the Harish Rawat government was revived following the victory in floor test held in Uttarakhand Legislative Assembly.</p>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Legislative_Assembly_election,_2017" title="Uttarakhand Legislative Assembly election, 2017">2017 Legislative Assembly election</a>, on 18 March 2017 Trivendra Singh Rawat sworn as the 8th Chief Minister of Uttarakhand of Fourth Assembly (2017–22).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sub-divisions">Sub-divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sub-divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kumaon_Garhwal.jpg"><img alt="Map of Uttarkhand" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="572" data-file-width="650" height="264" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Kumaon_Garhwal.jpg/300px-Kumaon_Garhwal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Kumaon_Garhwal.jpg/450px-Kumaon_Garhwal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Kumaon_Garhwal.jpg/600px-Kumaon_Garhwal.jpg 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kumaon_Garhwal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Districts_of_Uttarakhand" title="Districts of Uttarakhand">Districts of Uttarakhand</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Uttarakhand" title="Administrative divisions of Uttarakhand">Administrative divisions of Uttarakhand</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Districts_of_Uttarakhand" title="Districts of Uttarakhand">Districts of Uttarakhand</a></div>
<p>There are 13 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Districts_of_Uttarakhand" title="Districts of Uttarakhand">districts in Uttarakhand</a> which are grouped into two divisions, Kumaon and Garhwal. Four new districts named Didihat, Ranikhet, Kotdwar, and Yamunotri were declared by then Chief Minister of Uttarakhand, <a href="/wiki/Ramesh_Pokhriyal" title="Ramesh Pokhriyal">Ramesh Pokhriyal</a>, on 15 August 2011 but yet to be officially formed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup></p>
<p>Districts of two divisions are as follows:</p>
<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style=";border-spacing:0;background:transparent;">
<tr style="vertical-align:top;">
<td style="width:auto;;{{{col1style}}};">
<p><b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kumaon_Division" title="Kumaon Division">Kumaon Division</a></b></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Almora_district" title="Almora district">Almora</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bageshwar_District" title="Bageshwar District">Bageshwar</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Champawat_district" title="Champawat district">Champawat</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nainital_district" title="Nainital district">Nainital</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pithoragarh_district" title="Pithoragarh district">Pithoragarh</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Udham_Singh_Nagar_district" title="Udham Singh Nagar district">Udham Singh Nagar</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
<td style="width:1.25em;"></td>
<td style="width:auto;;{{{col2style}}};">

<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dehradun_district" title="Dehradun district">Dehradun</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haridwar_District" title="Haridwar District">Haridwar</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tehri_Garhwal" title="Tehri Garhwal">Tehri Garhwal</a> (commonly known as Tehri)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uttarkashi_District" title="Uttarkashi District">Uttarkashi</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chamoli_district" title="Chamoli district">Chamoli</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pauri_Garhwal" title="Pauri Garhwal">Pauri Garhwal</a> (commonly known as Pauri)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Rudraprayag_district" title="Rudraprayag district">Rudraprayag</a></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Each district is governed by a district collector or district magistrate. The districts are further divided into sub-divisions, which are governed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sub-Divisional_Magistrate" title="Sub-Divisional Magistrate">sub-divisional magistrates</a>; sub-divisions comprise blocks containing panchayats (village councils) and town municipalities.</p>
<p>According to the 2011 census, Haridwar, Dehradun, and Udham Singh Nagar are the most populous districts, each of them having a population of over one million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-census-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Uttarakhand" title="Music of Uttarakhand">Music of Uttarakhand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sumitra_nandan_pant_museum,_kausani.jpg"><img alt="Sumitranandan Pant museum, Kausani" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Sumitra_nandan_pant_museum%2C_kausani.jpg/220px-Sumitra_nandan_pant_museum%2C_kausani.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Sumitra_nandan_pant_museum%2C_kausani.jpg/330px-Sumitra_nandan_pant_museum%2C_kausani.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Sumitra_nandan_pant_museum%2C_kausani.jpg/440px-Sumitra_nandan_pant_museum%2C_kausani.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<p>Uttarakhand's diverse ethnicities have created a rich literary tradition in languages including Hindi, Kumaoni, Garhwali, Jaunsari, and Bhoti. Many of its traditional tales originated in the form of lyrical ballads and chanted by itinerant singers and are now considered classics of Hindi literature. <a href="/wiki/Ganga_Prasad_Vimal" title="Ganga Prasad Vimal">Ganga Prasad Vimal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manohar_Shyam_Joshi" title="Manohar Shyam Joshi">Manohar Shyam Joshi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prasoon_Joshi" title="Prasoon Joshi">Prasoon Joshi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shekhar_Joshi" title="Shekhar Joshi">Shekhar Joshi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shailesh_Matiyani" title="Shailesh Matiyani">Shailesh Matiyani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shivani" title="Shivani">Shivani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sangeet_Natak_Akademi_Award" title="Sangeet Natak Akademi Award">Sangeet Natak Akademi Awardee</a> <a href="/wiki/Mohan_Upreti" title="Mohan Upreti">Mohan Upreti</a>, <a href="/wiki/B._M._Shah" title="B. M. Shah">B. M. Shah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sahitya_Akademi_Award" title="Sahitya Akademi Award">Sahitya Akademi awardee</a> <a href="/wiki/Manglesh_Dabral" title="Manglesh Dabral">Manglesh Dabral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jnanpith_Award" title="Jnanpith Award">Jnanpith awardee</a> <a href="/wiki/Sumitranandan_Pant" title="Sumitranandan Pant">Sumitranandan Pant</a> are some major literary figures from the region. Prominent philosopher and environmental activist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sundarlal_Bahuguna" title="Sundarlal Bahuguna">Sundarlal Bahuguna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vandana_Shiva" title="Vandana Shiva">Vandana Shiva</a> are also from Uttarakhand, so is country music singer, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bobby_Cash_(singer)" title="Bobby Cash (singer)">Bobby Cash</a>.</p>
<p>The dances of the region are connected to life and human existence and exhibit myriad human emotions. Langvir Nritya is a dance form for males that resembles gymnastic movements. Barada Nati folk dance is another dance of <a href="/wiki/Jaunsar-Bawar" title="Jaunsar-Bawar">Jaunsar-Bawar</a>, which is practised during some religious festivals. Other well-known dances include Hurka Baul, Jhora-Chanchri, Jhumaila, Chauphula, and <a href="/wiki/Chholiya" title="Chholiya">Chholiya</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> Music is an integral part of the Uttarakhandi culture. Popular types of folk songs include Mangal, Basanti, Khuded and Chhopati.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> These folk songs are played on instruments including <a href="/wiki/Dhol" title="Dhol">dhol</a>, damau, turri, <a href="/wiki/Ransingha" title="Ransingha">ransingha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dholki" title="Dholki">dholki</a>, daur, <a href="/wiki/Thali" title="Thali">thali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhankora" title="Bhankora">bhankora</a>, mandan and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bagpipe" title="Bagpipe">mashakbaja</a>. "<a href="/wiki/Bedu_Pako" title="Bedu Pako">Bedu Pako</a>" is a popular folk song of Uttarakhand with international fame and legendary status within the state. It serves as the unofficial state anthem of Uttarakhand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> Music is also used as a medium through which the gods are invoked. <i><a href="/wiki/Jagar_(ritual)" title="Jagar (ritual)">Jagar</a></i> is a form of spirit worship in which the singer, or <i>Jagariya</i>, sings a ballad of the gods, with allusions to great epics, like <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mahabharat" title="Mahabharat">Mahabharat</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramayana" title="Ramayana">Ramayana</a>, that describe the adventures and exploits of the god being invoked. <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Singh_Negi" title="Narendra Singh Negi">Narendra Singh Negi</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mina_Rana" title="Mina Rana">Mina Rana</a> are popular folk singers of the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Architectural_details_of_a_Dharamshala,_estb._1822,_Haridwar.jpg"><img alt="building" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Architectural_details_of_a_Dharamshala%2C_estb._1822%2C_Haridwar.jpg/200px-Architectural_details_of_a_Dharamshala%2C_estb._1822%2C_Haridwar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Architectural_details_of_a_Dharamshala%2C_estb._1822%2C_Haridwar.jpg/300px-Architectural_details_of_a_Dharamshala%2C_estb._1822%2C_Haridwar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Architectural_details_of_a_Dharamshala%2C_estb._1822%2C_Haridwar.jpg/400px-Architectural_details_of_a_Dharamshala%2C_estb._1822%2C_Haridwar.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Architectural_details_of_a_Dharamshala,_estb._1822,_Haridwar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Architectural details of a Dharmashala, estb. 1822, Haridwar</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Abhisarika-nayika-mola-ram.jpg"><img alt="painting" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="532" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Abhisarika-nayika-mola-ram.jpg/150px-Abhisarika-nayika-mola-ram.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Abhisarika-nayika-mola-ram.jpg/225px-Abhisarika-nayika-mola-ram.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Abhisarika-nayika-mola-ram.jpg/300px-Abhisarika-nayika-mola-ram.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Abhisarika-nayika-mola-ram.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Abhisarika Nayika</i>, a painting by <a href="/wiki/Mola_Ram" title="Mola Ram">Mola Ram</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Among the prominent local crafts is wood carving, which appears most frequently in the ornately decorated temples of Uttarakhand. Intricately carved designs of floral patterns, deities, and geometrical motifs also decorate the doors, windows, ceilings, and walls of village houses. Paintings and murals are used to decorate both homes and temples. Pahari painting is a form of painting that flourished in the region between the 17th and 19th century. <a href="/wiki/Mola_Ram" title="Mola Ram">Mola Ram</a> started the Garhwal Branch of the <a href="/wiki/Kangra_painting" title="Kangra painting">Kangra school</a> of painting. <a href="/wiki/Guler_State" title="Guler State">Guler State</a> was known as the "cradle of Kangra paintings".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Kumaoni art often is geometrical in nature, while Garhwali art is known for its closeness to nature. Other crafts of Uttarakhand include handcrafted gold jewellery, basketry from Garhwal, woollen shawls, scarves, and rugs. The latter are mainly produced by the Bhotiyas of northern Uttarakhand.</p>
<p>The primary food of Uttarakhand is vegetables with wheat being a staple, although non-vegetarian food is also served. A distinctive characteristic of Uttarakhand cuisine is the sparing use of tomatoes, milk, and milk based products. Coarse grain with high fibre content is very common in Uttarakhand due to the harsh terrain. Another crop which is associated with Uttarakhand is <a href="/wiki/Buckwheat" title="Buckwheat">Buckwheat</a> (locally called <i>Madua</i> or <i>Jhingora</i>), particularly in the interior regions of Kumaon and Garhwal. Generally, either <a href="/wiki/Ghee" title="Ghee">Desi Ghee</a> or <a href="/wiki/Mustard_oil" title="Mustard oil">Mustard oil</a> is used for the purpose of cooking food. Simple recipes are made interesting with the use of hash seeds "Jakhiya" as spice. <a href="/wiki/Bal_Mithai" title="Bal Mithai">Bal Mithai</a> is a popular fudge-like sweet. Other popular dishes include Dubuk, Chains, Kap, Chutkani, Sei, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gulgula_sweet" title="Gulgula sweet">Gulgula</a>. A regional variation of <a href="/wiki/Kadhi" title="Kadhi">Kadhi</a> called <i>Jhoi</i> or <i>Jholi</i> is also popular.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:312px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bathing_ghat_on_the_Ganges_during_Kumbh_Mela,_2010,_Haridwar.jpg"><img alt="Kumbh Mela" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="335" data-file-width="762" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bathing_ghat_on_the_Ganges_during_Kumbh_Mela%2C_2010%2C_Haridwar.jpg/310px-Bathing_ghat_on_the_Ganges_during_Kumbh_Mela%2C_2010%2C_Haridwar.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bathing_ghat_on_the_Ganges_during_Kumbh_Mela%2C_2010%2C_Haridwar.jpg/465px-Bathing_ghat_on_the_Ganges_during_Kumbh_Mela%2C_2010%2C_Haridwar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Bathing_ghat_on_the_Ganges_during_Kumbh_Mela%2C_2010%2C_Haridwar.jpg/620px-Bathing_ghat_on_the_Ganges_during_Kumbh_Mela%2C_2010%2C_Haridwar.jpg 2x" width="310"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bathing_ghat_on_the_Ganges_during_Kumbh_Mela,_2010,_Haridwar.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bathing ghat on the Ganges during Kumbh Mela, 2010, Haridwar</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>One of the major Hindu pilgrimages, <a href="/wiki/Haridwar_Kumbh_Mela" title="Haridwar Kumbh Mela">Haridwar Kumbh Mela</a>, takes place in Uttarakhand. <a href="/wiki/Haridwar" title="Haridwar">Haridwar</a> is one of the four places in India where this mela is organised. Haridwar most recently hosted the Purna Kumbh Mela from <a href="/wiki/Makar_Sankranti" title="Makar Sankranti">Makar Sankranti</a> (14 January 2010) to Vaishakh Purnima Snan (28 April 2010). Hundreds of foreigners joined Indian pilgrims in the festival which is considered the largest religious gathering in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AFP_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-AFP-51">[51]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kumauni_Holi" title="Kumauni Holi">Kumauni Holi</a>, in forms including Baithki Holi, Khari Holi and Mahila Holi, all of which start from <a href="/wiki/Vasant_Panchami" title="Vasant Panchami">Vasant Panchami</a>, are festivals and musical affairs that can last almost a month. Ganga Dashahara, Vasant Panchami, Makar Sankranti, Ghee Sankranti, Khatarua, Vat Savitri, and Phul Dei are other major festivals. In addition, various fairs like <a href="/wiki/Kanwar_Yatra" title="Kanwar Yatra">Kanwar Yatra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kandali_Festival" title="Kandali Festival">Kandali Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ramman_(festival)" title="Ramman (festival)">Ramman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harela_mela" title="Harela mela">Harela mela</a>, Nauchandi mela, Uttarayani mela and <a href="/wiki/Nanda_Devi_Raj_Jat" title="Nanda Devi Raj Jat">Nanda Devi Raj Jat Mela</a> take place.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Uttarakhand" title="Economy of Uttarakhand">Economy of Uttarakhand</a></div>
<p>The Uttarakhand state is the second fastest growing state in India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> It's gross state domestic product (GSDP) (at constant prices) more than doubled from <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>24,786 crore in FY2005 to <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>60,898 crore in FY2012. The real GSDP grew at 13.7% (CAGR) during the FY2005–FY2012 period. The contribution of the service sector to the GSDP of Uttarakhand was just over 50% during FY 2012. Per capita income in Uttarakhand is <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>1,03,000 (FY 2013) which is higher than the national average of <span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>74,920 (FY2013).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_Bank_of_India" title="Reserve Bank of India">Reserve Bank of India</a>, the total foreign direct investment in the state from April 2000 to October 2009 amounted to US$46.7 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vannage_du_riz,_Uttarakhand,_India.jpg"><img alt="Rice winnowing" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4320" data-file-width="3240" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Vannage_du_riz%2C_Uttarakhand%2C_India.jpg/150px-Vannage_du_riz%2C_Uttarakhand%2C_India.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Vannage_du_riz%2C_Uttarakhand%2C_India.jpg/225px-Vannage_du_riz%2C_Uttarakhand%2C_India.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Vannage_du_riz%2C_Uttarakhand%2C_India.jpg/300px-Vannage_du_riz%2C_Uttarakhand%2C_India.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vannage_du_riz,_Uttarakhand,_India.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A lady winnowing rice, an important food crop in Uttarakhand.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Like most of India, agriculture is one of the most significant sectors of the economy of Uttarakhand. <a href="/wiki/Basmati" title="Basmati">Basmati</a> rice, wheat, soybeans, groundnuts, coarse cereals, pulses, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oil_seeds" title="Oil seeds">oil seeds</a> are the most widely grown crops. Fruits like apples, oranges, pears, peaches, litchis, and plums are widely grown and important to the large food processing industry. Agricultural export zones have been set up in the state for leechi, horticulture, herbs, medicinal plants, and basmati rice. During 2010, wheat production was 831 thousand tonnes and rice production was 610 thousand tonnes, while the main cash crop of the state, sugarcane, had a production of 5058 thousand tonnes. As 86% of the state consists of hills, the yield per hectare is not very high. 86% of all croplands are in the plains while the remaining is from the hills.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phd_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-phd-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<table cellspacing="1" class="wikitable" style="float:right; width:260px; margin:0 0 1em 1em; background:#f4f5f6; border:#c6c7c8 solid; font-size:90%;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="background:#c2d6e5; text-align:center;">Economy of Uttarakhand at a Glance<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mospi.nic.in_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-mospi.nic.in-57">[57]</a></sup>
<p>figures in <a href="/wiki/Crore" title="Crore">crores</a> of <a href="/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">Indian rupees</a></p>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th>Economy at a Glance (FY-2012)</th>
<th>In Indian rupees</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>GSDP (current)</td>
<td><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>95,201</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Per capita income</td>
<td><span style="white-space: nowrap">₹</span>1,03,000</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Other key industries include tourism and hydropower, and there is prospective development in IT, ITES, biotechnology, pharmaceuticals and automobile industries. The service sector of Uttarakhand mainly includes tourism, information technology, higher education, and banking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-phd_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-phd-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>During 2005–2006, the state successfully developed three Integrated Industrial Estates (IIEs) at <a href="/wiki/Haridwar" title="Haridwar">Haridwar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pantnagar" title="Pantnagar">Pantnagar</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sitarganj" title="Sitarganj">Sitarganj</a>; Pharma City at Selaqui; Information Technology Park at Sahastradhara (<a href="/wiki/Dehradun" title="Dehradun">Dehradun</a>); and a growth centre at Siggadi (<a href="/wiki/Kotdwar" title="Kotdwar">Kotdwar</a>). Also in 2006, 20 industrial sectors in public private partnership mode were developed in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ppp_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ppp-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
