</table>
<p>Uttarakhand has a diversity of flora and fauna. It has a recorded forest area of 34,666 km<sup>2</sup> which constitutes 65% of the total area of the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Uttarakhand is home to rare species of plants and animals, many of which are protected by sanctuaries and reserves. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_parks_of_India" title="National parks of India">National parks</a> in Uttarakhand include the <a href="/wiki/Jim_Corbett_National_Park" title="Jim Corbett National Park">Jim Corbett National Park</a> (the oldest national park of India) at <a href="/wiki/Ramnagar,_Uttarakhand" title="Ramnagar, Uttarakhand">Ramnagar</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nainital_District" title="Nainital District">Nainital District</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Flowers_National_Park" title="Valley of Flowers National Park">Valley of Flowers National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nanda_Devi_National_Park" title="Nanda Devi National Park">Nanda Devi National Park</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chamoli_District" title="Chamoli District">Chamoli District</a>, which together are a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>. A number of plant species in the valley are internationally threatened, including several that have not been recorded from elsewhere in Uttarakhand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-unesco335_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-unesco335-63">[63]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rajaji_National_Park" title="Rajaji National Park">Rajaji National Park</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haridwar_District" title="Haridwar District">Haridwar District</a> and <a href="/wiki/Govind_Pashu_Vihar_National_Park_and_Sanctuary" title="Govind Pashu Vihar National Park and Sanctuary">Govind Pashu Vihar National Park and Sanctuary</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gangotri_National_Park" title="Gangotri National Park">Gangotri National Park</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uttarkashi_District" title="Uttarkashi District">Uttarkashi District</a> are some other protected areas in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wildlife_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-wildlife-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Spotted_deers_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2933" data-file-width="4885" height="132" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Spotted_deers_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park.JPG/220px-Spotted_deers_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Spotted_deers_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park.JPG/330px-Spotted_deers_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Spotted_deers_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park.JPG/440px-Spotted_deers_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Spotted_deers_in_Jim_Corbett_National_Park.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Chital" title="Chital">Chital</a> crossing forest path at <a href="/wiki/Jim_Corbett_National_Park" title="Jim Corbett National Park">Jim Corbett National Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leopards" title="Leopards">Leopards</a> are found in areas which are abundant in hills but may also venture into the lowland jungles. Smaller felines include the <a href="/wiki/Jungle_cat" title="Jungle cat">jungle cat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fishing_cat" title="Fishing cat">fishing cat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Leopard_cat" title="Leopard cat">leopard cat</a>. Other mammals include four kinds of deer (<a href="/wiki/Muntjac" title="Muntjac">barking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sambar_deer" title="Sambar deer">sambar</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hog_deer" title="Hog deer">hog</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chital" title="Chital">chital</a>), <a href="/wiki/Sloth_bear" title="Sloth bear">sloth</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asiatic_black_bear" title="Asiatic black bear">Himalayan black bears</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_gray_mongoose" title="Indian gray mongoose">Indian gray mongooses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otter" title="Otter">otters</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martes_flavigula" title="Martes flavigula">yellow-throated martens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bharal" title="Bharal">bharal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indian_pangolin" title="Indian pangolin">Indian pangolins</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Langur" title="Langur">langur</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhesus_macaque" title="Rhesus macaque">rhesus</a> monkeys. In the summer, <a href="/wiki/Asian_elephant" title="Asian elephant">elephants</a> can be seen in <a href="/wiki/Herd" title="Herd">herds</a> of several hundred. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marsh_crocodile" title="Marsh crocodile">Marsh crocodiles</a> (<i>Crocodylus palustris</i>), <a href="/wiki/Gharial" title="Gharial">gharials</a> (<i>Gavialis gangeticus</i>) and other reptiles are also found in the region. Local crocodiles were saved from extinction by captive breeding programs and subsequently re-released into the <a href="/wiki/Ramganga" title="Ramganga">Ramganga</a> river.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Several freshwater terrapins and turtles like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_sawback_turtle" title="Indian sawback turtle">Indian sawback turtle</a> (<i>Kachuga tecta</i>), <a href="/wiki/Brahminy_river_turtle" title="Brahminy river turtle">brahminy river turtle</a> (<i>Hardella thurgii</i>), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ganges_softshell_turtle" title="Ganges softshell turtle">Ganges softshell turtle</a> (<i>Trionyx gangeticus</i>) are found in the rivers. Butterflies and birds of the region include <a href="/wiki/Papilio_helenus" title="Papilio helenus">red Helen</a> (<i>Papilio helenus</i>), the <a href="/wiki/Hypolimnas_bolina" title="Hypolimnas bolina">great eggfly</a> (<i>Hypolimnos bolina</i>), <a href="/wiki/Danaus_genutia" title="Danaus genutia">common tiger</a> (<i>Danaus genutia</i>), <a href="/wiki/Pareronia_avatar" title="Pareronia avatar">pale wanderer</a> (<i>Pareronia avatar avatar</i>), <a href="/wiki/Jungle_babbler" title="Jungle babbler">jungle babbler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tawny-bellied_babbler" title="Tawny-bellied babbler">tawny-bellied babbler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_slaty_woodpecker" title="Great slaty woodpecker">great slaty woodpecker</a>, <a href="/wiki/Red-breasted_parakeet" title="Red-breasted parakeet">red-breasted parakeet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orange-breasted_green_pigeon" title="Orange-breasted green pigeon">orange-breasted green pigeon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chestnut-winged_cuckoo" title="Chestnut-winged cuckoo">chestnut-winged cuckoo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sharma1998_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sharma1998-66">[66]</a></sup> In 2011, a rare migratory bird, the <a href="/wiki/Bean_goose" title="Bean goose">bean goose</a>, was also seen in the <a href="/wiki/Jim_Corbett_National_Park" title="Jim Corbett National Park">Jim Corbett National Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-corbett_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-corbett-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">Evergreen oaks</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rhododendrons" title="Rhododendrons">rhododendrons</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conifers" title="Conifers">conifers</a> predominate in the hills. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sal_(tree)" title="Sal (tree)">sal</a></i> (<i>Shorea robusta</i>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silk_cotton_tree" title="Silk cotton tree">silk cotton tree</a> (<i>Bombax ciliata</i>), <i><a href="/wiki/Dalbergia_sissoo" title="Dalbergia sissoo">Dalbergia sissoo</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mallotus_philippensis" title="Mallotus philippensis">Mallotus philippensis</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acacia_catechu" title="Acacia catechu">Acacia catechu</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bauhinia_racemosa" title="Bauhinia racemosa">Bauhinia racemosa</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Bauhinia_variegata" title="Bauhinia variegata">Bauhinia variegata</a></i> (camel's foot tree) are some other trees of the region. <i><a href="/wiki/Albizia_chinensis" title="Albizia chinensis">Albizia chinensis</a></i>, the sweet sticky flowers of which are favoured by sloth bears, are also part of the region's flora.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sharma1998_66-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sharma1998-66">[66]</a></sup> A decade long study by Prof. <a href="/wiki/Chandra_Prakash_Kala" title="Chandra Prakash Kala">Chandra Prakash Kala</a> concluded that the Valley of Flowers is endowed with 520 species of higher plants (<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angiosperms" title="Angiosperms">angiosperms</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gymnosperms" title="Gymnosperms">gymnosperms</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pteridophytes" title="Pteridophytes">pteridophytes</a></i>), of these 498 are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Flowering_plants" title="Flowering plants">flowering plants</a>. The park has many species of medicinal plants including <i><a href="/wiki/Dactylorhiza_hatagirea" title="Dactylorhiza hatagirea">Dactylorhiza hatagirea</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Picrorhiza_kurroa" title="Picrorhiza kurroa">Picrorhiza kurroa</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Aconitum_violaceum" title="Aconitum violaceum">Aconitum violaceum</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Polygonatum_multiflorum" title="Polygonatum multiflorum">Polygonatum multiflorum</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fritillaria_roylei" title="Fritillaria roylei">Fritillaria roylei</a></i>, and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Podophyllum_hexandrum" title="Podophyllum hexandrum">Podophyllum hexandrum</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> In the summer season of 2016, a large portion of forests in Uttarakhand caught fires and rubbled to ashes during <a href="/wiki/2016_Uttarakhand_forest_fires" title="2016 Uttarakhand forest fires">Uttarakhand forest fires</a> incident which resulted in the damage of forest resources worth billions of rupees and death of 6 people with hundreds of wild animals died during fires.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dehradun_Airport_Terminal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2045" data-file-width="3062" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Dehradun_Airport_Terminal.jpg/320px-Dehradun_Airport_Terminal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Dehradun_Airport_Terminal.jpg/480px-Dehradun_Airport_Terminal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Dehradun_Airport_Terminal.jpg/640px-Dehradun_Airport_Terminal.jpg 2x" width="320"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dehradun_Airport_Terminal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jolly_Grant_Airport" title="Jolly Grant Airport">Jolly Grant Airport</a>, Dehradun</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Uttarakhand has 28,508 km of roads, of which 1,328 km are national highways and 1,543 km are state highways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ppp_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-ppp-58">[58]</a></sup> The State Road Transport Corporation (SRTC), which has been reorganised in Uttarakhand as the <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Transport_Corporation" title="Uttarakhand Transport Corporation">Uttarakhand Transport Corporation</a>, is a major constituent of the transport system in the state. The Corporation began to work on 31 October 2003 and provides services on interstate and nationalised routes. As of 2012, approximately 1000 buses are being plied by the "Uttarakhand Transport Corporation" on 35 nationalised routes along with many other non-nationalised routes. There are also private transport operators operating approximately 3000 buses on non-nationalised routes along with a few interstate routes in Uttarakhand and the neighbouring state of U.P.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> For travelling locally, the state, like most of the country, has <a href="/wiki/Auto_rickshaw" title="Auto rickshaw">auto rickshaws</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cycle_rickshaw" title="Cycle rickshaw">cycle rickshaws</a>. In addition, remote towns and villages in the hills are connected to important road junctions and bus routes by a vast network of crowded share jeeps.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>The air transport network in the state is gradually improving. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jolly_Grant_Airport" title="Jolly Grant Airport">Jolly Grant Airport</a> in Dehradun, is the busiest airport in the state with six daily flights to <a href="/wiki/Indira_Gandhi_International_Airport" title="Indira Gandhi International Airport">Delhi Airport</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pantnagar_Airport" title="Pantnagar Airport">Pantnagar Airport</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Pantnagar" title="Pantnagar">Pantnagar</a> of the Kumaon region have 1 daily air service to delhi and return too . There government is planning to develop <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naini_Saini_Airport" title="Naini Saini Airport">Naini Saini Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pithoragarh" title="Pithoragarh">Pithoragarh</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bharkot_Airport" title="Bharkot Airport">Bharkot Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Chinyalisaur" title="Chinyalisaur">Chinyalisaur</a> in Uttarkashi district and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gauchar_Airport" title="Gauchar Airport">Gauchar Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gauchar" title="Gauchar">Gauchar</a>, Chamoli district. There are plans to launch helipad service in Pantnagar and Jolly Grant Airports and other important tourist destinations like <a href="/wiki/Ghangaria" title="Ghangaria">Ghangaria</a> and Hemkund Sahib.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>As over 86% of Uttarakhand's terrain consists of hills, railway services are very limited in the state and are largely confined to the plains. In 2011, the total length of railway tracks was about 345 km.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ppp_58-2"><a href="#cite_note-ppp-58">[58]</a></sup> Rail, being the cheapest mode of transport, is most popular. The most important railway station in Kumaun Division of Uttarakhand is at <a href="/wiki/Kathgodam" title="Kathgodam">Kathgodam</a>, 35 kilometres away from Nainital. Kathgodam is the last terminus of the broad gauge line of North East Railways that connects Nainital with Delhi, Dehradun, and Howrah. Other notable railway stations are at <a href="/wiki/Pantnagar" title="Pantnagar">Pantnagar</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lalkuan" title="Lalkuan">Lalkuan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Haldwani" title="Haldwani">Haldwani</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Dehradun_railway_station" title="Dehradun railway station">Dehradun railway station</a> is a railhead of the Northern Railways.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> Haridwar station is situated on the Delhi–Dehradun and Howrah–Dehradun railway lines. One of the main railheads of the Northern Railways, Haridwar Junction Railway Station is connected by broad gauge line. Roorkee comes under Northern Railway region of Indian Railways on the main <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_India" title="Punjab, India">Punjab</a> – <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mughal_Sarai" title="Mughal Sarai">Mughal Sarai</a> trunk route and is connected to major Indian cities. Other railheads are <a href="/wiki/Rishikesh" title="Rishikesh">Rishikesh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kotdwar" title="Kotdwar">Kotdwar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ramnagar,_Uttarakhand" title="Ramnagar, Uttarakhand">Ramnagar</a> linked to Delhi by daily trains.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Uttarakhand" title="Tourism in Uttarakhand">Tourism in Uttarakhand</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schematic_Tourist_Map_of_Uttarakhand.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Schematic_Tourist_Map_of_Uttarakhand.jpg/220px-Schematic_Tourist_Map_of_Uttarakhand.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Schematic_Tourist_Map_of_Uttarakhand.jpg/330px-Schematic_Tourist_Map_of_Uttarakhand.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Schematic_Tourist_Map_of_Uttarakhand.jpg/440px-Schematic_Tourist_Map_of_Uttarakhand.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schematic_Tourist_Map_of_Uttarakhand.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Tourist map</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Uttarakhand has many tourist spots due to its location in the Himalayas. There are many ancient temples, forest reserves, national parks, hill stations, and mountain peaks that draw large number of tourists. There are 44 nationally protected monuments in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oak_Grove_School_(Jharipani,_Mussoorie)" title="Oak Grove School (Jharipani, Mussoorie)">Oak Grove School</a> in the state is on the tentative list for World Heritage Sites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> Two of the most holy rivers in <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hinduism</a> the <a href="/wiki/Ganges" title="Ganges">Ganges</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yamuna" title="Yamuna">Yamuna</a>, originate in Uttarakhand.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ali_bugyal2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Ali_bugyal2.jpg/250px-Ali_bugyal2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Ali_bugyal2.jpg/375px-Ali_bugyal2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Ali_bugyal2.jpg/500px-Ali_bugyal2.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ali_bugyal2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bugyal" title="Bugyal">Bugyal</a> (meadow) in Uttarakhand</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hemkunt-003.jpg"><img alt="a pilgrimage site for Sikhs" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1125" data-file-width="1500" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Hemkunt-003.jpg/220px-Hemkunt-003.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Hemkunt-003.jpg/330px-Hemkunt-003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Hemkunt-003.jpg/440px-Hemkunt-003.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hemkunt-003.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hemkund" title="Hemkund">Gurdwara Hemkund Sahib</a>, an important pilgrimage site for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sikhs" title="Sikhs">Sikhs</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Uttarakhand has long been called "Land of the Gods"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uttarakhand_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-Uttarakhand-29">[29]</a></sup> as the state has some of the holiest <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">Hindu</a> shrines, and for more than a thousand years, pilgrims have been visiting the region in the hopes of salvation and purification from sin. <a href="/wiki/Gangotri" title="Gangotri">Gangotri</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yamunotri" title="Yamunotri">Yamunotri</a>, the sources of the Ganges and Yamuna, dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Ganges_in_Hinduism" title="Ganges in Hinduism">Ganga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yamuna_in_Hinduism" title="Yamuna in Hinduism">Yamuna</a> respectively, fall in the upper reaches of the state and together with <a href="/wiki/Badrinath" title="Badrinath">Badrinath</a> (dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Kedarnath" title="Kedarnath">Kedarnath</a> (dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Shiva" title="Shiva">Shiva</a>) form the <a href="/wiki/Chota_Char_Dham" title="Chota Char Dham">Chota Char Dham</a>, one of Hinduism's most spiritual and auspicious pilgrimage circuits. Haridwar, meaning "Gateway to the God", is a prime Hindu destination. Haridwar hosts the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kumbha_Mela" title="Kumbha Mela">Kumbha Mela</a> every twelve years, in which millions of pilgrims take part from all parts of India and the world. <a href="/wiki/Rishikesh" title="Rishikesh">Rishikesh</a> near Haridwar is known as the preeminent yoga centre of India. The state has an abundance of temples and shrines, many dedicated to local deities or manifestations of Shiva and <a href="/wiki/Durga" title="Durga">Durga</a>, references to many of which can be found in Hindu scriptures and legends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Uttarakhand is, however, a place of pilgrimage not only for Hindus. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piran_Kaliyar" title="Piran Kaliyar">Piran Kaliyar Sharif</a> near <a href="/wiki/Roorkee" title="Roorkee">Roorkee</a> is a pilgrimage site to <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hemkund" title="Hemkund">Gurdwara Hemkund Sahib</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanakmatta" title="Nanakmatta">Gurdwara Nanakmatta Sahib</a> and Gurdwara Reetha Sahib are pilgrimage centers for <a href="/wiki/Sikh" title="Sikh">Sikhs</a>. <a href="/wiki/Tibetan_Buddhism" title="Tibetan Buddhism">Tibetan Buddhism</a> has also made its presence with the reconstruction of <a href="/wiki/Mindrolling_Monastery#Mindrolling_in_India" title="Mindrolling Monastery">Mindrolling Monastery</a> and its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Buddha" title="Buddha">Buddha</a> <a href="/wiki/Stupa" title="Stupa">Stupa</a>, described as the world's highest at <a href="/wiki/Clement_Town" title="Clement Town">Clement Town</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dehradun" title="Dehradun">Dehradun</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some of the most well-known hill stations in India are in Uttarakhand.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Mussoorie" title="Mussoorie">Mussoorie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nainital" title="Nainital">Nainital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dhanaulti" title="Dhanaulti">Dhanaulti</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chakrata" title="Chakrata">Chakrata</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tehri" title="Tehri">Tehri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lansdowne,_India" title="Lansdowne, India">Lansdowne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pauri" title="Pauri">Pauri</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sattal" title="Sattal">Sattal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Almora" title="Almora">Almora</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kausani" title="Kausani">Kausani</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bhimtal" title="Bhimtal">Bhimtal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ranikhet" title="Ranikhet">Ranikhet</a> are some popular hill stations in Uttarakhand. <a href="/wiki/Auli" title="Auli">Auli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Munsiari" title="Munsiari">Munsiari</a> are well-known skiing resorts in the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The state has 12 National Parks and Wildlife Sanctuaries which cover 13.8 percent of the total area of the state. They are located at different altitudes varying from 800 to 5400 metres. The oldest national park on the Indian sub-continent, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Corbett_National_Park" title="Jim Corbett National Park">Jim Corbett National Park</a>, is a major tourist attraction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wildlife_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-wildlife-64">[64]</a></sup> The park has varied wildlife and <a href="/wiki/Project_Tiger" title="Project Tiger">Project Tiger</a> run by the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India" title="Government of India">Government of India</a>. <a href="/wiki/Rajaji_National_Park" title="Rajaji National Park">Rajaji National Park</a> is known for its elephants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In addition, the state boasts <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Flowers_National_Park" title="Valley of Flowers National Park">Valley of Flowers National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nanda_Devi_National_Park" title="Nanda Devi National Park">Nanda Devi National Park</a> in Chamoli District, which together are a UNESCO World Heritage Site. <a href="/wiki/Vasudhara_Falls" title="Vasudhara Falls">Vasudhara Falls</a>, near <a href="/wiki/Badrinath" title="Badrinath">Badrinath</a> is a waterfall with a height of 122 metres (400 ft) set in a backdrop of snow-clad mountains.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harsh_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-harsh-81">[81]</a></sup> The state has always been a destination for <a href="/wiki/Mountaineering" title="Mountaineering">mountaineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">hiking</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rock_climbing" title="Rock climbing">rock climbing</a> in India. A recent development in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adventure_tourism" title="Adventure tourism">adventure tourism</a> in the region has been whitewater <a href="/wiki/Rafting" title="Rafting">rafting</a> in Rishikesh. Due to its proximity to the Himalaya ranges, the place is full of hills and mountains and is suitable for trekking, climbing, skiing, camping, rock climbing, and paragliding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roopkund" title="Roopkund">Roopkund</a> is a trekking site, known for the mysterious skeletons found in a lake, which was featured by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Geographic_Channel" title="National Geographic Channel">National Geographic Channel</a> in a documentary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> The trek to Roopkund passes through the meadows of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bugyal" title="Bugyal">Bugyal</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Uttarakhand" title="Education in Uttarakhand">Education in Uttarakhand</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_institutions_of_higher_education_in_Uttarakhand" title="List of institutions of higher education in Uttarakhand">List of institutions of higher education in Uttarakhand</a></div>
<p>On 30 September 2010 there were 15,331 primary schools with 1,040,139 students and 22,118 working teachers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> At the 2011 census the literacy rate of the state was 78.82% with 87.40% literacy for males and 70.01% literacy for females.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Demography_37-4"><a href="#cite_note-Demography-37">[37]</a></sup> The language of instruction in the schools is either English or Hindi. There are mainly government-run, private unaided (no government help), and private aided schools in the state. The main school affiliations are <a href="/wiki/Central_Board_of_Secondary_Education" title="Central Board of Secondary Education">CBSE</a>, <a href="/wiki/Council_for_the_Indian_School_Certificate_Examinations" title="Council for the Indian School Certificate Examinations">CISCE</a> or <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Board_of_School_Education" title="Uttarakhand Board of School Education">UBSE</a>, the state syllabus defined by the Department of Education of the Government of Uttarakhand.</p>
<p>Uttarakhand is also home to a number of universities and degree colleges. Dehradun is known as school capital of India.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The high mountains and rivers of Uttarakhand attract many tourists and adventure seekers. It is also a favorite destination for <a href="/wiki/Extreme_sport" title="Extreme sport">adventure sports</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Paragliding" title="Paragliding">paragliding</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sky_diving" title="Sky diving">sky diving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rafting" title="Rafting">rafting</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bungee_jumping" title="Bungee jumping">bungee jumping</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup></p>
<p>More recently, golf has also become popular, with <a href="/wiki/Ranikhet" title="Ranikhet">Ranikhet</a> being a favorite destination.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_Cricket_Association" title="Uttarakhand Cricket Association">Uttarakhand Cricket Association</a> is the governing body for cricket activities and the Uttarakhand Cricket Team.</p>
<p>The Uttarakhand Football Association is the governing body for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Association_Football" title="Association Football">Association Football</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Uttarakhand_football_team" title="Uttarakhand football team">Uttarakhand football team</a> represents Uttarakhand in the <a href="/wiki/Santosh_Trophy" title="Santosh Trophy">Santosh Trophy</a> and other leagues.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports_stadiums">Sports stadiums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Uttarakhand&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sports stadiums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
